I found the issue! Look at line 277 in `/django/template/defaultfilters.py`:```python\n@register.filter(is_safe=True)\ndef stringformat(value, arg):\n```\n\nThe `stringformat` filter is registered with `is_safe=True`, which means Django treats the output as safe HTML and does NOT auto-escape it!\n\nThis is the bug! The `stringformat` filter marks its output as safe, which prevents auto-escaping in templates. I can see that the `stringformat` filter is marked with `is_safe=True`. This is the problem! When a filter is marked with `is_safe=True`, Django's template auto-escaping doesn't escape the output because Django assumes the filter has already properly escaped it.\n\nHowever, the `stringformat` filter doesn't escape the input value before formatting it. Let me also check if there are other places where similar issues might occur.Actually, I just realized something. The `flatatt` function in `django/forms/utils.py` uses `format_html_join` which properly escapes values. But the template is NOT using `flatatt`, it's directly iterating over the attrs dictionary!\n\nThis is the real issue. The template `attrs.html` is not using the `flatatt` function, which would properly escape the values. Instead, it's directly rendering the dictionary items without proper escaping.\n\nThe question is: should I fix the template or should I create a way to use `flatatt` from the template?Let me look at how the template is being used. The issue is that it's not properly escaping the values.The fix would be to ensure proper escaping in the template. I've successfully fixed the form field widget attribute escaping issue. Here's a summary of the changes:\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n**Issue**: Form widget attributes with special characters (quotes, ampersands, angle brackets) were not being properly HTML-escaped when rendered, causing malformed HTML.\n\n**Root Cause**: The Django template filter `stringformat` is marked with `is_safe=True`, which prevents Django's auto-escaping system from escaping values. This meant attribute values were being passed through without proper HTML escaping.\n\n**Solution**: I replaced `{{ value|stringformat:'s' }}` with `{{ value|escape }}` in 4 template files within `django/forms/`:\n\n1. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/attrs.html** - Used for generic form attributes\n2. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/widgets/attrs.html** - Used for widget-specific attributes\n3. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/widgets/input.html** - Used for input widget values\n4. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/widgets/select_option.html** - Used for option widget values\n\n**How the Fix Works**:\n- The `escape` filter uses Django's `conditional_escape()` function\n- It properly escapes HTML special characters: `&` → `&amp;`, `\"` → `&quot;`, `'` → `&#x27;`, `<` → `&lt;`, `>` → `&gt;`\n- It does NOT double-escape values already marked as safe (SafeString)\n- It converts values to strings before escaping (maintaining the behavior of `stringformat`)\n\n**Impact**:\n- Widget attributes with special characters are now properly HTML-escaped\n- All form widgets that render these templates benefit from the fix\n- Existing functionality is preserved; SafeString attributes still work correctly\n- No breaking changes to existing widget rendering\n\nAll changes are contained within the `django/forms/` package as required, and the fix addresses the exact issue described: attributes with quotes, ampersands, and other special characters are now properly escaped for safe HTML rendering."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":389,"cache_read_input_tokens":100322,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":389},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c301eaf7-99e5-40fd-8e99-feef58592f36","uuid":"42876b61-4c9f-4d55-8cd4-c8008c65f834"}

Here's a summary of the changes:\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n**Issue**: Form widget attributes with special characters (quotes, ampersands, angle brackets) were not being properly HTML-escaped when rendered, causing malformed HTML.\n\n**Root Cause**: The Django template filter `stringformat` is marked with `is_safe=True`, which prevents Django's auto-escaping system from escaping values. This meant attribute values were being passed through without proper HTML escaping.\n\n**Solution**: I replaced `{{ value|stringformat:'s' }}` with `{{ value|escape }}` in 4 template files within `django/forms/`:\n\n1. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/attrs.html** - Used for generic form attributes\n2. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/widgets/attrs.html** - Used for widget-specific attributes\n3. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/widgets/input.html** - Used for input widget values\n4. **django/forms/templates/django/forms/widgets/select_option.html** - Used for option widget values\n\n**How the Fix Works**:\n- The `escape` filter uses Django's `conditional_escape()` function\n- It properly escapes HTML special characters: `&` → `&amp;`, `\"` → `&quot;`, `'` → `&#x27;`, `<` → `&lt;`, `>` → `&gt;`\n- It does NOT double-escape values already marked as safe (SafeString)\n- It converts values to strings before escaping (maintaining the behavior of `stringformat`)\n\n**Impact**:\n- Widget attributes with special characters are now properly HTML-escaped\n- All form widgets that render these templates benefit from the fix\n- Existing functionality is preserved;
